<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_architecture">Culture and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_in_Dresden" title="Culture in Dresden">Culture in Dresden</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_pano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dresden_pano.jpg/220px-Dresden_pano.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dresden_pano.jpg/330px-Dresden_pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dresden_pano.jpg/440px-Dresden_pano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_pano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dresden at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg/220px-Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg/330px-Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg/440px-Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_silhouette.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dresden_Frauenkirche" title="Dresden Frauenkirche">Dresden Frauenkirche</a>, symbol of Dresden</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carl_Maria_von_Weber" title="Carl Maria von Weber">Carl Maria von Weber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a> had a number of their works performed for the first time in Dresden.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other famous artists, such as <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Ludwig_Kirchner" title="Ernst Ludwig Kirchner">Ernst Ludwig Kirchner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otto_Dix" title="Otto Dix">Otto Dix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Kokoschka" title="Oskar Kokoschka">Oskar Kokoschka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">Richard Strauss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Semper" title="Gottfried Semper">Gottfried Semper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gret_Palucca" title="Gret Palucca">Gret Palucca</a>, were also active in the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Dresden is also home to several important art collections, world-famous musical ensembles, and significant buildings from various <a href="/wiki/Architectural_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Architectural history">architectural periods</a>, many of which were rebuilt after the destruction of the Second World War.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg/220px-Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg/330px-Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg/440px-Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1366" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_-_Semperoper_-_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Semperoper" title="Semperoper">Semperoper</a>, completely rebuilt and reopened in 1985</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden,Yenidze_(11382419176).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Dresden%2CYenidze_%2811382419176%29.jpg/220px-Dresden%2CYenidze_%2811382419176%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Dresden%2CYenidze_%2811382419176%29.jpg/330px-Dresden%2CYenidze_%2811382419176%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Dresden%2CYenidze_%2811382419176%29.jpg/440px-Dresden%2CYenidze_%2811382419176%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden,Yenidze_(11382419176).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Yenidze" title="Yenidze">Yenidze</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Saxon State Opera descends from the opera company of the former electors and Kings of Saxony. Their first opera house was the <a href="/wiki/Opernhaus_am_Taschenberg" title="Opernhaus am Taschenberg">Opernhaus am Taschenberg</a>, opened in 1667. The <a href="/wiki/Opernhaus_am_Zwinger" title="Opernhaus am Zwinger">Opernhaus am Zwinger</a> presented opera from 1719 to 1756, when the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> began. The later <a href="/wiki/Semperoper" title="Semperoper">Semperoper</a> was completely destroyed during the bombing of Dresden during the second world war. The opera's reconstruction was completed exactly 40 years later, on 13 February 1985. Its musical ensemble is the <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A4chsische_Staatskapelle_Dresden" class="mw-redirect" title="Sächsische Staatskapelle Dresden">Sächsische Staatskapelle Dresden</a></i>, founded in 1548.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Staatsschauspiel_Dresden" title="Staatsschauspiel Dresden">Dresden State Theatre</a> runs a number of smaller theatres. The Dresden State Operetta is the only independent <a href="/wiki/Operetta" title="Operetta">operetta</a> in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The <i>Herkuleskeule</i> (<a href="/wiki/Hercules" title="Hercules">Hercules</a> <a href="/wiki/Club_(weapon)" title="Club (weapon)">club</a>) is an important site in <a href="/wiki/Kabarett" title="Kabarett">German-speaking political cabaret</a>.</p>
<p>There are several choirs in Dresden, the best-known of which is the <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_Kreuzchor" title="Dresdner Kreuzchor">Dresdner Kreuzchor</a> (Choir of <a href="/wiki/Christian_cross" title="Christian cross">The Holy Cross</a>). It is a boys' choir drawn from pupils of the <a href="/wiki/Kreuzschule" title="Kreuzschule">Kreuzschule</a>, and was founded in the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The <i>Dresdner Kapellknaben</i> are not related to the <i>Staatskapelle</i>, but to the former <i>Hofkapelle</i>, the Catholic cathedral, since 1980. The <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Philharmonic_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Dresden Philharmonic Orchestra">Dresden Philharmonic Orchestra</a> is the orchestra of the city of Dresden.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Throughout the summer, the outdoor concert series "Zwingerkonzerte und Mehr" is held in the <a href="/wiki/Zwinger_(Dresden)" title="Zwinger (Dresden)"><i>Zwingerhof</i></a>. Performances include dance and music.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>A big event each year in June is the <a href="/wiki/Bunte_Republik_Neustadt" title="Bunte Republik Neustadt">Bunte Republik Neustadt</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> a culture festival lasting 3 days in the city district of <a href="/wiki/Innere_Neustadt_(Dresden)" title="Innere Neustadt (Dresden)">Dresden-Neustadt</a>. Bands play live concerts for free in the streets and people can find all kinds of refreshments and food.</p>
<h3><span id="Museums,_presentations_and_collections"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums.2C_presentations_and_collections">Museums, presentations and collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Museums, presentations and collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dresden hosts the <a href="/wiki/Staatliche_Kunstsammlungen_Dresden" title="Staatliche Kunstsammlungen Dresden"><i>Staatlichen Kunstsammlungen Dresden</i></a> (Dresden State Art Collections) which, according to the institution's own statements, place it among the most important museums presently in existence. The art collections consist of twelve museums, of which the <i><a href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie_Alte_Meister" title="Gemäldegalerie Alte Meister">Gemäldegalerie Alte Meister</a></i> (Old Masters Gallery) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnes_Gew%C3%B6lbe" title="Grünes Gewölbe">Grünes Gewölbe</a></i> (Green Vault) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Japanese_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Palace">Japanese Palace</a></i> (Japanisches Palais) are the most famous.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Also known are <i><a href="/wiki/Galerie_Neue_Meister" title="Galerie Neue Meister">Galerie Neue Meister</a></i> (New Masters Gallery), <i><a href="/wiki/Dresden_Armory" title="Dresden Armory">Rüstkammer</a></i> (Armoury) with the <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Armory#Turkish_Chamber" title="Dresden Armory">Turkish Chamber</a>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Dresden_Museum_of_Ethnology" title="Dresden Museum of Ethnology">Museum für Völkerkunde Dresden</a></i> (Museum of Ethnology). Other museums and collections owned by the Free State of Saxony in Dresden are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/German_Hygiene_Museum" title="German Hygiene Museum">Deutsche Hygiene-Museum</a></i>, founded for <a href="/wiki/Mass_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass education">mass education</a> in hygiene, health, <a href="/wiki/Human_biology" title="Human biology">human biology</a> and medicine<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i>Landesmuseum für Vorgeschichte</i> (State Museum of Prehistory)<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <i>Staatliche Naturhistorische Sammlungen Dresden</i> (State Collection of Natural History)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>The <i>Universitätssammlung Kunst + Technik</i> (Collection of Art and Technology of the Dresden University of Technology)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Dresden_Transport_Museum" title="Dresden Transport Museum">Verkehrsmuseum Dresden</a></i> (Transport Museum)</li>
<li><i>Festung Dresden</i> (Dresden Fortress)<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dresden_City_Museum" title="Dresden City Museum">Dresden City Museum</a> is run by the city of Dresden and focused on the city's history. The <i><a href="/wiki/Milit%C3%A4rhistorisches_Museum_der_Bundeswehr" class="mw-redirect" title="Militärhistorisches Museum der Bundeswehr">Militärhistorisches Museum der Bundeswehr</a></i> (Military History Museum) is placed in the former garrison in the Albertstadt.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The book museum of the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_State_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Saxon State Library">Saxon State Library</a> presents the famous <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Codex" title="Dresden Codex">Dresden Codex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WDL_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-75">[75]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_der_Technischen_Universit%C3%A4t_Dresden" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanischer Garten der Technischen Universität Dresden"><i>Botanischer Garten Dresden</i></a> is a botanical garden in the <i><a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fer_Garten" title="Großer Garten">Großer Garten</a></i> that is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/Dresden_University_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Dresden University of Technology">Dresden University of Technology</a>. Also located in the <i>Großer Garten</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Zoo" title="Dresden Zoo">Dresden Zoo</a>.</p>
<p>The Kraszewski-Museum is a museum dedicated to the most prolific <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a> writer <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Ignacy_Kraszewski" title="Józef Ignacy Kraszewski">Józef Ignacy Kraszewski</a>, who lived in Dresden from 1863 to 1883.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although Dresden is often said to be a Baroque city, its architecture is influenced by more than one style. Other eras of importance are the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Historism" title="Historism">Historism</a>, as well as the contemporary styles of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">Modernism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Postmodernism" title="Postmodernism">Postmodernism</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Dresden has some 13&#160;000 listed cultural monuments and eight districts under general preservation orders.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_household">Royal household</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Royal household">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG/220px-Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG/330px-Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG/440px-Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-Zwinger.courtyard.04.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Zwinger_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Zwinger Palace">Zwinger Palace</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The royal buildings are among the most impressive buildings in Dresden. The <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Castle" title="Dresden Castle">Dresden Castle</a> was the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Household" title="Royal Household">royal household</a> from 1485. The wings of the building have been renewed, built upon and restored many times. Due to this integration of styles, the castle is made up of elements of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classicism" title="Classicism">Classicist</a> styles.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Zwinger_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Zwinger Palace">Zwinger Palace</a> is across the road from the castle. It was built on the old stronghold of the city and was converted to a centre for the royal art collections and a place to hold festivals. Its gate by the moat, surmounted by a golden crown, is famous.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other royal buildings and ensembles:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BChl%27s_Terrace" title="Brühl's Terrace">Brühl's Terrace</a> was a gift to <a href="/wiki/Heinrich,_count_von_Br%C3%BChl" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinrich, count von Brühl">Heinrich, count von Brühl</a>, and became an ensemble of buildings above the river Elbe.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dresden_Elbe_Valley" title="Dresden Elbe Valley">Dresden Elbe Valley</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Pillnitz_Castle" title="Pillnitz Castle">Pillnitz Castle</a> and other castles</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sacred_buildings">Sacred buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sacred buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe,_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe%2C_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe%2C_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe%2C_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe%2C_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe%2C_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe%2C_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6175" data-file-height="3486" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canaletto_-_Dresden_seen_from_the_Right_Bank_of_the_Elbe,_beneath_the_Augusts_Bridge_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Bellotto" title="Bernardo Bellotto">Bernardo Bellotto</a>'s Dresden included the <a href="/wiki/Katholische_Hofkirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Katholische Hofkirche">Hofkirche</a> during construction.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Katholische_Hofkirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Katholische Hofkirche">Hofkirche</a> was the church of the royal household. Augustus the Strong, who desired to be <a href="/wiki/King_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Poland">King of Poland</a>, converted to Catholicism, as Polish kings had to be Catholic. At that time Dresden was strictly Protestant. Augustus the Strong ordered the building of the Hofkirche, the Roman Catholic Cathedral, to establish a sign of Roman Catholic religious importance in Dresden. The church is the cathedral "Sanctissimae Trinitatis" since 1980. The crypt of the <a href="/wiki/Wettin_(dynasty)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wettin (dynasty)">Wettin Dynasty</a> is located within the church.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> King <a href="/wiki/Augustus_III_of_Poland" title="Augustus III of Poland">Augustus III of Poland</a> is buried in the Cathedral, as one of very few <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">Polish Kings</a> to be buried outside the <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Cathedral" title="Wawel Cathedral">Wawel Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>.</p>
<p>In contrast to the Hofkirche, the Lutheran <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Frauenkirche" title="Dresden Frauenkirche">Frauenkirche</a> was built almost contemporaneously by the citizens of Dresden. It is said to be the greatest cupola building in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and Northern Europe. The city's historic Kreuzkirche was reconsecrated in 1388.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are also other churches in Dresden, for example a <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> in the Südvorstadt district.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_architecture">Contemporary architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Contemporary architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg/220px-Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg/330px-Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg/440px-Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3276" data-file-height="2244" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-Kristallpalast-nigh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The locally controversial UFA-Palast</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dresden has been an important site for the development of <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_architecture" title="Contemporary architecture">contemporary architecture</a> for centuries, and this trend has continued into the 20th and 21st centuries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Historicism_(art)" title="Historicism (art)">Historicist</a> buildings made their presence felt on the cityscape until the 1920s sampled by public buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A4chsische_Staatskanzlei" title="Sächsische Staatskanzlei">Staatskanzlei</a> or the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden_City_Hall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dresden City Hall (page does not exist)">City Hall</a>. One of the youngest buildings of that era is the Hygiene Museum, which is designed in an impressively monumental style, but employs plain façades and simple structures. It is often attributed, wrongly, to the <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a> school.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Most of the present cityscape of Dresden was built after 1945, a mix of reconstructed or repaired old buildings and new buildings in the modern and postmodern styles. Important buildings erected between 1945 and 1990 are the Centrum-Warenhaus (a large <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department store</a>) representing the <a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">international Style</a>, the Kulturpalast, and several smaller and two bigger complexes of <a href="/wiki/Plattenbau" title="Plattenbau">Plattenbau</a> housing in <a href="/wiki/Gorbitz" title="Gorbitz">Gorbitz</a>, while there is also housing dating from the era of <a href="/wiki/Stalinist_architecture" title="Stalinist architecture">Stalinist architecture</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg/220px-Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg/330px-Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg/440px-Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="672" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_synagoge_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The New Synagogue</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After 1990 and German reunification, new styles emerged. Important contemporary buildings include the <a href="/wiki/New_Synagogue,_Dresden" title="New Synagogue, Dresden">New Synagogue</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_architecture" title="Postmodern architecture">postmodern</a> building with few windows, the <a href="/wiki/Transparent_Factory" title="Transparent Factory">Transparent Factory</a>, the Saxon State Parliament and the New Terrace, the UFA-Kristallpalast cinema by <a href="/wiki/Coop_Himmelb(l)au" title="Coop Himmelb(l)au">Coop Himmelb(l)au</a> (one of the biggest buildings of <a href="/wiki/Deconstructivism" title="Deconstructivism">Deconstructivism</a> in Germany), and the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_State_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Saxon State Library">Saxon State Library</a>. <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Libeskind" title="Daniel Libeskind">Daniel Libeskind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster,_Baron_Foster_of_Thames_Bank" title="Norman Foster, Baron Foster of Thames Bank">Norman Foster</a> both modified existing buildings. Foster roofed the main railway station with translucent Teflon-coated synthetics. Libeskind changed the whole structure of the <a href="/wiki/Bundeswehr_Military_History_Museum" title="Bundeswehr Military History Museum">Bundeswehr Military History Museum</a> Museum by placing a wedge through the historical arsenal building.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_buildings">Other buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG/220px-Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG/330px-Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG/440px-Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1152" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Goldener_Reiter_Dresden_Germany.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The gilded equestrian sculpture of <a href="/wiki/Augustus_II_the_Strong" title="Augustus II the Strong">August the Strong</a> of Poland and Saxony</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other buildings include important bridges crossing the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a> river, the <a href="/wiki/Blaues_Wunder" class="mw-redirect" title="Blaues Wunder">Blaues Wunder</a> bridge and the <a href="/wiki/Augustusbr%C3%BCcke" class="mw-redirect" title="Augustusbrücke">Augustusbrücke</a>, which is on the site of the oldest bridge in Dresden.</p>
<p>There are about 300 fountains and springs, many of them in parks or squares. The wells serve only a decorative function, since there is a <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a> system in Dresden. Springs and fountains are also elements in contemporary cityspaces.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The most famous sculpture in Dresden is <a href="/wiki/Jean-Joseph_Vinache" title="Jean-Joseph Vinache">Jean-Joseph Vinache</a>'s golden <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_sculpture" class="mw-redirect" title="Equestrian sculpture">equestrian sculpture</a> of August the Strong called the <i>Goldener Reiter</i> (Golden Cavalier) on the Neustädter Markt square. It shows August at the beginning of the Hauptstraße (Main street) on his way to Warsaw, where he was King of Poland in personal union. Another sculpture is the memorial of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> in front of the Frauenkirche.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span id="Dresden-Hellerau—Germany's_first_garden_city"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dresden-Hellerau.E2.80.94Germany.27s_first_garden_city">Dresden-Hellerau—Germany's first garden city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Dresden-Hellerau—Germany's first garden city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Garden_city_movement" title="Garden city movement">Garden City</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hellerau" title="Hellerau">Hellerau</a>, at that time a suburb of Dresden, was founded in 1909. In 1911 <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Tessenow" title="Heinrich Tessenow">Heinrich Tessenow</a> built the Hellerau <a href="/wiki/Festspielhaus_Hellerau" title="Festspielhaus Hellerau">Festspielhaus</a> (festival theatre) and Hellerau became a centre of modernism with international standing until the outbreak of World War I.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1950, Hellerau was incorporated into the city of Dresden. Today the Hellerau reform architecture is recognized as exemplary. In the 1990s, the garden city of Hellerau became a <a href="/wiki/Conservation_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservation area">conservation area</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Living_quarters">Living quarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Living quarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Dresden's urban parts are subdivided in rather a lot of city quarters, up to around 100, among them relatively many larger villa quarters dominated by historic multiple dwelling units, especially, but not only along the river, most known are <a href="/wiki/Blasewitz" title="Blasewitz">Blasewitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loschwitz" title="Loschwitz">Loschwitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pillnitz" title="Pillnitz">Pillnitz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wei%C3%9Fer_Hirsch" class="mw-redirect" title="Weißer Hirsch">Weißer Hirsch</a>. Also some Art Nouveau living quarters and two bigger quarters typical for communist architecture&#160;– but much renovated&#160;– can be found. The villa town of <a href="/wiki/Radebeul" title="Radebeul">Radebeul</a> joins the Dresden city tram system, which is expansive due to the lack of an underground system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinemas_and_cinematics">Cinemas and cinematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cinemas and cinematics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are several small <a href="/wiki/Cinemas" class="mw-redirect" title="Cinemas">cinemas</a> presenting <a href="/wiki/Cult_film" title="Cult film">cult films</a> and low-budget or low-profile films chosen for their cultural value. Dresden also has a few multiplex cinemas, of which the Rundkino is the oldest.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Dresden has been a centre for the production of animated films and optical <a href="/wiki/Cinematic_techniques" title="Cinematic techniques">cinematic techniques</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg/250px-Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg" width="250" height="103" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg/375px-Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg/500px-Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="886" data-file-height="364" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rudolf-Harbig-Stadion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Gl%C3%BCcksgas_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Glücksgas Stadium">Glücksgas Stadium</a>, the current home of Dynamo Dresden</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dresden is home to <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Dresden" title="Dynamo Dresden">Dynamo Dresden</a>, which had a tradition in <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_and_Champions_League_history" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup and Champions League history">UEFA club competitions</a> up to the early 1990s. Dynamo Dresden won eight titles in the <a href="/wiki/DDR-Oberliga" title="DDR-Oberliga">DDR-Oberliga</a>. Currently, the club is a member of the <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a> after some seasons in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> and <a href="/wiki/3rd_Liga" class="mw-redirect" title="3rd Liga">3rd Liga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the early 20th century, the city was represented by <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_SC" title="Dresdner SC">Dresdner SC</a>, who were one of Germany's most successful clubs in football. Their best performances came during World War II, when they were twice German <a href="/wiki/German_football_champions" class="mw-redirect" title="German football champions">champions</a>, and twice <a href="/wiki/DFB_Pokal" class="mw-redirect" title="DFB Pokal">Cup</a> winners. Dresdner SC is a multisport club. While its <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football team</a> plays in the sixth-tier <a href="/wiki/Landesliga_Sachsen" class="mw-redirect" title="Landesliga Sachsen">Landesliga Sachsen</a>, its volleyball section has a team in the women's <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bundesliga_(volleyball)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bundesliga (volleyball) (page does not exist)">Bundesliga</a>. Dresden has a third <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> <a href="/wiki/Team" title="Team">team</a> <a href="/wiki/SC_Borea_Dresden" title="SC Borea Dresden">SC Borea Dresden</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_Eisl%C3%B6wen" title="Dresdner Eislöwen">ESC Dresdner Eislöwen</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> club playing in the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Bundesliga_(ice_hockey)" title="2nd Bundesliga (ice hockey)">2nd Bundesliga</a> again. <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Monarchs" title="Dresden Monarchs">Dresden Monarchs</a> are an <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team in the <a href="/wiki/German_Football_League" title="German Football League">German Football League</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Titans" title="Dresden Titans">Dresden Titans</a> are the city's top basketball team. Due to good performances, they have moved up several divisions and currently play in Germany's second division <a href="/wiki/ProA" title="ProA">ProA</a>. The Titans' home arena is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Margon_Arena&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Margon Arena (page does not exist)">Margon Arena</a>.</p>
<p>Since 1890, <a href="/wiki/Horse_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse race">horse races</a> have taken place and the Dresdener Rennverein 1890 e.V. are active and one of the big sporting events in Dresden.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Major sporting facilities in Dresden are the <a href="/wiki/Gl%C3%BCcksgas_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Glücksgas Stadium">Glücksgas Stadium</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Heinz-Steyer-Stadion" title="Heinz-Steyer-Stadion">Heinz-Steyer-Stadion</a> and the <a href="/wiki/EnergieVerbund_Arena" title="EnergieVerbund Arena">EnergieVerbund Arena</a> for <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</div>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Dresden" title="Transportation in Dresden">Transportation in Dresden</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NGTD12DD_front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/NGTD12DD_front.jpg/220px-NGTD12DD_front.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/NGTD12DD_front.jpg/330px-NGTD12DD_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/NGTD12DD_front.jpg/440px-NGTD12DD_front.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NGTD12DD_front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The longest trams in Dresden set a record in length</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_4" title="Bundesautobahn 4">Bundesautobahn 4</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_route_E40" title="European route E40">European route E40</a>) crosses Dresden in the northwest from west to east. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_17" title="Bundesautobahn 17">Bundesautobahn 17</a> leaves the A4 in a south-eastern direction. In Dresden it begins to cross the Ore Mountains towards Prague. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_13" title="Bundesautobahn 13">Bundesautobahn 13</a> leaves from the three-point interchange "Dresden-Nord" and goes to Berlin. The A13 and the A17 are on the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E55" title="European route E55">European route E55</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe" title="Bundesstraße">Bundesstraße</a> roads crossing or running through Dresden.</p>
<p>There are two main inter-city transit hubs in the railway network in Dresden: <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Hauptbahnhof" title="Dresden Hauptbahnhof">Dresden Hauptbahnhof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dresden-Neustadt_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Dresden-Neustadt railway station">Dresden-Neustadt railway station</a>. The most important railway lines run to Berlin, Prague, Leipzig and Chemnitz. A <a href="/wiki/Regional_rail" title="Regional rail">commuter train</a> system (<a href="/wiki/Dresden_S-Bahn" title="Dresden S-Bahn">Dresden S-Bahn</a>) operates on three lines alongside the long-distance routes.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dresden_Airport" title="Dresden Airport">Dresden Airport</a> is the city's <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a>, located at the north-western outskirts of the town. Its infrastructure has been improved<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> with new terminals and a motorway access route.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG/220px-Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG/330px-Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG/440px-Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1989" data-file-height="1193" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden_Mainstation_2007_04_23.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dresden_Hauptbahnhof" title="Dresden Hauptbahnhof">Dresden Central Station</a> is the main inter-city transport hub</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dresden has a large tramway network operated by <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_Verkehrsbetriebe" title="Dresdner Verkehrsbetriebe">Dresdner Verkehrsbetriebe</a>, the municipal transport company. Because the geological bedrock does not allow the building of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">underground railways</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> the tramway is an important form of public transport. The Transport Authority operates twelve lines on a 200&#160;km (124&#160;mi) network.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Many of the new <a href="/wiki/Low_floor" class="mw-redirect" title="Low floor">low-floor</a> vehicles are up to 45 metres long and produced by <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier Transportation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bautzen" title="Bautzen">Bautzen</a>. While about 30&#160;% of the system's lines are on <a href="/wiki/Reserved_track" title="Reserved track">reserved track</a> (often sown with grass to avoid noise), many tracks still run on the streets, especially in the inner city.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/CarGoTram" title="CarGoTram">CarGoTram</a> is a tram that supplies Volkswagen's <a href="/wiki/Transparent_Factory" title="Transparent Factory">Transparent Factory</a>, crossing the city. The transparent factory is located not far from the city centre next to the city's largest park.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The districts of Loschwitz and Weisser Hirsch are connected by the <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Funicular_Railway" title="Dresden Funicular Railway">Dresden Funicular Railway</a>, which has been carrying passengers back and forth since 1895.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_utilities">Public utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Public utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg/220px-Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg/330px-Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg/440px-Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3650" data-file-height="1862" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-Kultusministerium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A4chsische_Staatskanzlei" title="Sächsische Staatskanzlei">Sächsische Staatskanzlei</a> (<i>Saxon State Chancellery</i>) is an institution assisting the President of the State</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dresden is the capital of a German <i><a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">Land</a></i> (federal state). It is home to the <a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_Saxony" class="mw-redirect" title="Landtag of Saxony">Landtag of Saxony</a><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and the ministries of the Saxon Government. The controlling <a href="/wiki/List_of_constitutional_courts" class="mw-redirect" title="List of constitutional courts">Constitutional Court</a> of Saxony is in Leipzig. The highest Saxon court in civil and <a href="/wiki/Criminal_law" title="Criminal law">criminal law</a>, the Higher Regional Court of Saxony, has its home in Dresden.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the Saxon state authorities are located in Dresden. Dresden is home to the Regional Commission of the <a href="/wiki/Dresden_(region)" title="Dresden (region)">Dresden Regierungsbezirk</a>, which is a controlling authority for the Saxon Government. It has jurisdiction over eight <a href="/wiki/List_of_rural_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rural districts of Germany">rural districts</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Urban_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban districts of Germany">urban districts</a> and the city of Dresden.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Like many cities in Germany, Dresden is also home to a local court, has a trade corporation and a Chamber of Industry and Trade and many subsidiaries of federal agencies (such as the Federal Labour Office or the <a href="/wiki/Technisches_Hilfswerk" title="Technisches Hilfswerk">Federal Agency for Technical Relief</a>). It hosts some divisions of the German Customs and the eastern Federal Waterways Directorate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Dresden is home to a military subdistrict command, but no longer has large military units as it did in the past. Dresden is the traditional location for <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">army officer</a> schooling in Germany, today carried out in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Offizierschule_des_Heeres&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Offizierschule des Heeres (page does not exist)">Offizierschule des Heeres</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Dresden" title="Economy of Dresden">Economy of Dresden</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg/220px-Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg/330px-Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg/440px-Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1120" data-file-height="840" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_AMD_Dresden_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Advanced_Micro_Devices" title="Advanced Micro Devices">Advanced Micro Devices</a> factory</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg/220px-Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg" width="220" height="91" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg/330px-Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg/440px-Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1270" data-file-height="524" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kongresszentrum_Dresden2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The International Congress Center Dresden</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Until famous enterprises like <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_Bank" title="Dresdner Bank">Dresdner Bank</a> left Dresden in the communist era to avoid <a href="/wiki/Nationalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalisation">nationalisation</a>, Dresden was one of the most important German cities, an important industrial centre of the German Democratic Republic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The period of the <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="German Democratic Republic">GDR</a> until 1990 was characterized by low economic growth in comparison to western German cities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1990 Dresden had to struggle with the <a href="/wiki/Economic_collapse" title="Economic collapse">economic collapse</a> of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">the Soviet Union</a> and the other export markets in Eastern Europe. After reunification enterprises and production sites broke down almost completely as they entered the <a href="/wiki/Social_market_economy" title="Social market economy">social market economy</a>, facing competition from the Federal Republic of Germany. After 1990 a completely new <a href="/wiki/Legal_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal system">legal system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> system was introduced and infrastructure was largely rebuilt with funds from the Federal Republic of Germany. Dresden as a major urban centre has developed much faster and more consistently than most other regions in the former German Democratic Republic, but it still faces many social and economic problems stemming from the collapse of the former system, including high unemployment levels.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Between 1990 and 2010 the <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment rate</a> fluctuated between 13% and 15% and is still relatively high, with a low of 8.9% in May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Dresden has raised its <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP per capita</a> to 31,100 euro, close to the GDP per capita of some West German communities (the average of the 50 biggest cities is around 35,000 euro).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thanks to the presence of public administration centres, a high density of semi-public research institutes and an extension of publicly funded high technology sectors, the proportion of highly qualified workers Dresden is again among the highest in Germany and by European criteria. Dresden regularly ranks among the best ten bigger cities in Germany to live in.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG/220px-Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG/330px-Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG/440px-Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glaeserne_Manufaktur_Dresden.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Transparent_Factory" title="Transparent Factory">Transparent Factory</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enterprises">Enterprises</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Enterprises">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Three major sectors dominate Dresden's economy:</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Silicon_Saxony" title="Silicon Saxony">Silicon Saxony</a> Saxony's semiconductor industry was built up in 1969. Major enterprises today are <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Micro_Devices" title="Advanced Micro Devices">AMD</a>'s spin-off <a href="/wiki/GLOBALFOUNDRIES" class="mw-redirect" title="GLOBALFOUNDRIES">GLOBALFOUNDRIES</a>, <a href="/wiki/Infineon_Technologies" title="Infineon Technologies">Infineon Technologies</a>, <a href="/wiki/ZMDI" title="ZMDI">ZMDI</a> and Toppan Photomasks. Their factories attract many suppliers of material and cleanroom technology enterprises to Dresden.</p>
<p>The pharmaceutical sector developed at the end of the 19th century. The 'Sächsisches Serumwerk Dresden' (Saxon Serum Plant, Dresden), owned by <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>, is a global leader in <a href="/wiki/Vaccine" title="Vaccine">vaccine</a> production.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Another traditional pharmaceuticals producer is Arzneimittelwerke Dresden (Pharmaceutical Works, Dresden).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A third traditional branch is that of mechanical and <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>. Major employers are the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> <a href="/wiki/Transparent_Factory" title="Transparent Factory">Transparent Factory</a>, <a href="/wiki/EADS" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS">EADS</a> <a href="/wiki/EADS_EFW" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS EFW">Elbe Flugzeugwerke</a> (Elbe Aircraft Works), <a href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens AG">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Linde_Group" title="The Linde Group">Linde-KCA-Dresden</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>The tourism industry enjoys high revenue and supports many employees. There are around one hundred bigger hotels in Dresden, many of which cater in the upscale range.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Dresden still has a shortage of corporate headquarters.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The media sector is not particularly strong in Dresden.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The media in Dresden include two major newspapers of regional record: the <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A4chsische_Zeitung" title="Sächsische Zeitung">Sächsische Zeitung</a></i> (<i>Saxon Newspaper</i>, circulation around 228,000) and the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresdner_Neueste_Nachrichten&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dresdner Neueste Nachrichten (page does not exist)">Dresdner Neueste Nachrichten</a></i> (<i>Dresden's Latest News</i>, circulation around 50,000). Dresden has a broadcasting centre belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Mitteldeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Mitteldeutscher Rundfunk">Mitteldeutscher Rundfunk</a>. The <i>Dresdner Druck- und Verlagshaus</i> (Dresden printing plant and publishing house) produces part of <a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Spiegel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Print_run" class="mw-redirect" title="Print run">print run</a>, amongst other newspapers and magazines.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education and science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-Frauenkirche-View.from.top.03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Dresden-Frauenkirche-View.from.top.03.JPG/220px-Dresden-Frauenkirche-View.from.top.03.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Dresden-Frauenkirche-View.from.top.03.JPG/330px-Dresden-Frauenkirche-View.from.top.03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Dresden-Frauenkirche-View.from.top.03.JPG/440px-Dresden-Frauenkirche-View.from.top.03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
