<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dresden is home to a number of renowned universities, but among German cities it is a more recent location for academic education.</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Dresden_University_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Dresden University of Technology">Dresden University of Technology</a> (Technische Universität Dresden) with more than 36,000 students (2011)<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> was founded in 1828 and is among the oldest and largest <a href="/wiki/University_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Technology">Universities of Technology</a> in Germany. It is currently the university of technology in Germany with the largest number of students but also has many courses in <a href="/wiki/Social_studies" title="Social studies">social studies</a>, economics and other non-technical sciences. It offers 126 courses. In 2006, the TU Dresden was successful in the <a href="/wiki/German_Universities_Excellence_Initiative" title="German Universities Excellence Initiative">German Universities Excellence Initiative</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Education_and_Research_(Germany)" title="Federal Ministry of Education and Research (Germany)">Federal Ministry of Education and Research (Germany)</a>.</li>
<li>The Dresden University of Technology founded a Kids-University in 2004.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden_University_of_Applied_Sciences&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dresden University of Applied Sciences (page does not exist)">Dresden University of Applied Sciences</a> (Hochschule für Technik und Wirtschaft Dresden) was founded in 1992 and had about 5,300 students in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Academy_of_Fine_Arts" title="Dresden Academy of Fine Arts">Dresden Academy of Fine Arts</a> (Hochschule für Bildende Künste Dresden) was founded in 1764 and is known for its former professors and artists such as <a href="/wiki/George_Grosz" title="George Grosz">George Grosz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sascha_Schneider" title="Sascha Schneider">Sascha Schneider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otto_Dix" title="Otto Dix">Otto Dix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Kokoschka" title="Oskar Kokoschka">Oskar Kokoschka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Bellotto" title="Bernardo Bellotto">Bernardo Bellotto</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carl-Gustav_Carus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carl-Gustav Carus (page does not exist)">Carl-Gustav Carus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caspar_David_Friedrich" title="Caspar David Friedrich">Caspar David Friedrich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Richter" title="Gerhard Richter">Gerhard Richter</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Palucca_School_of_Dance" title="Palucca School of Dance">Palucca School of Dance</a> (Palucca Hochschule für Tanz)<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Gret_Palucca" title="Gret Palucca">Gret Palucca</a> in 1925 and is a major European school of <a href="/wiki/Free_dance" title="Free dance">free dance</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Musik_Carl_Maria_von_Weber_Dresden" class="mw-redirect" title="Hochschule für Musik Carl Maria von Weber Dresden">Carl Maria von Weber College of Music</a> was founded in 1856.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other universities include the "Hochschule für Kirchenmusik", a school specialising in <a href="/wiki/Christian_music" title="Christian music">church music</a>, the "Evangelische Hochschule für Sozialarbeit", an education institution for <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">social work</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The "Dresden International University" is a private postgraduate university, founded a few years ago<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> in cooperation with the Dresden University of Technology.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-WTC-night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Dresden-WTC-night.jpg/220px-Dresden-WTC-night.jpg" width="220" height="313" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Dresden-WTC-night.jpg/330px-Dresden-WTC-night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Dresden-WTC-night.jpg/440px-Dresden-WTC-night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2328" data-file-height="3315" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dresden-WTC-night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dresden World Trade Centre at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_institutes">Research institutes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Research institutes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dresden hosts many <a href="/wiki/Research_institute" title="Research institute">research institutes</a>, some of which have gained an international standing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The domains of most importance are micro- and nanoelectronics, transport and infrastructure systems, material and photonic technology, and bio-engineering. The institutes are well connected among one other as well as with the academic education institutions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Helmholtz-Zentrum_Dresden-Rossendorf" title="Helmholtz-Zentrum Dresden-Rossendorf">Helmholtz-Zentrum Dresden-Rossendorf</a> is the largest complex of research facilities in Dresden, a short distance outside the urban areas. It focuses on <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_medicine" title="Nuclear medicine">nuclear medicine</a> and physics. As part of the <a href="/wiki/Helmholtz_Association_of_German_Research_Centres" title="Helmholtz Association of German Research Centres">Helmholtz Association</a> it is one of the German <a href="/wiki/Big_Science" title="Big Science">Big Science</a> research centres.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Society</a> focuses on <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">fundamental research</a>. In Dresden there are three Max Planck Institutes (MPI); the "<a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Molecular_Cell_Biology_and_Genetics" class="mw-redirect" title="Max Planck Institute for Molecular Cell Biology and Genetics">MPI of Molecular Cell Biology and Genetics</a>", the "MPI for <a href="/wiki/Chemical_physics" title="Chemical physics">Chemical Physics</a> of Solids" and the "<a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_the_Physics_of_Complex_Systems" title="Max Planck Institute for the Physics of Complex Systems">MPI for the Physics of Complex Systems</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Society</a> hosts institutes of applied research that also offer mission-oriented research to enterprises. With eleven institutions or parts of institutes, Dresden is the largest location of the Fraunhofer Society worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The Fraunhofer Society has become an important factor in location decisions and is seen as a useful part of the "knowledge infrastructure".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Wilhelm_Leibniz_Scientific_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz Scientific Community">Leibniz Community</a> is a union of institutes with science covering fundamental research and applied research. In Dresden there are three Leibniz Institutes. The "<a href="/wiki/Leibniz_Institute_for_Polymer_Research" title="Leibniz Institute for Polymer Research">Leibniz Institute for Polymer Research</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and the "<a href="/wiki/Leibniz_Institute_for_Solid_State_and_Materials_Research" class="mw-redirect" title="Leibniz Institute for Solid State and Materials Research">Leibniz Institute for Solid State and Materials Research</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> are both in the material and <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high-technology</a> domain, while the "Leibniz Institute for Ecological and Regional Development" is focused on more fundamental research into urban planning.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>Helmholtz-Zentrum Dresden-Rossendorf was member of the Leibniz Community until the end of 2010.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_secondary_education">Higher secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Higher secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dresden has<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> more than 20 <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(Germany)" title="Gymnasium (Germany)">Gymnasien</a> which prepare for a tertiary education, five of which are private.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The "Sächsisches Landesgymnasium für Musik" with a focus on music is supported, as its name implies by the State of Saxony, rather than by the city.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> There are some <i>Berufliche Gymnasien</i> which combine <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education</a> and secondary education and a <i>Abendgymnasium</i> which prepares higher education of adults avocational.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sons_and_daughters_of_the_town">Sons and daughters of the town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sons and daughters of the town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Christine Bergmann (born 1939), politician (SPD)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/August_Buchner" title="August Buchner">August Buchner</a> (1591–1661), influential Baroque poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erich_K%C3%A4stner" title="Erich Kästner">Erich Kästner</a> (1899–1974), author of books</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Victor_Klemperer" title="Victor Klemperer">Victor Klemperer</a> (1881-1960) Jewish author of "I Will Bear Witness"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siarhei_Mikhalok" title="Siarhei Mikhalok">Siarhei Mikhalok</a> (born 1972), Belarusian rock musician and actor</li>
<li>Wolfgang Mischnick (1921–2002), politician FDP</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_Reinisch" title="Karl Reinisch">Karl Reinisch</a> (1921–2007), engineer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Richter" title="Gerhard Richter">Gerhard Richter</a> (born 1932), painter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Helmut_Sch%C3%B6n" title="Helmut Schön">Helmut Schön</a> (1915–1996), football trainer, lead Germany to world championship in 1974</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Herbert_Wehner" title="Herbert Wehner">Herbert Wehner</a> (1906–1990), politician SPD</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dresden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
